397→}\n   398→\n   399→/*\n   400→ * Determine which type of backlight interface to use on this system,\n   401→ * First check cmdline, then dmi quirks, then do autodetect.\n   402→ *\n   403→ * The autodetect order is:\n   404→ * 1) Is the acpi-video backlight interface supported ->\n   405→ *  no, use a vendor interface\n   406→ * 2) Is this a win8 \"ready\" BIOS and do we have a native 433→\t\tinit_done = true;\n   434→\t}\n   435→\tmutex_unlock(&init_mutex);\n   436→\n   437→\tif (acpi_backlight_cmdline != acpi_backlight_undef)\n   438→\t\treturn acpi_backlight_cmdline;\n   439→\n If it's NOT vendor (i.e., it's video or native), then disable acer-wmi's brightness capability\n\nSo the logic is:\n- If the system is in video_vendor_dmi_table, set the backlight type to \"vendor\" via video_detect\n- If the backlight type is NOT \"vendor\", disable acer-wmi brightness\n\nFor the TravelMate 5735Z:\n- It's NOT in video_vendor_dmi_table, so step 1-2 don't apply\n- acpi_video_get_backlight_type() would return something (let's think about what)\n  - No cmdline parameter (by default)\n  - No DMI quirk set (since 5735Z is not in video_detect_dmi_table)\n  - Need to check if video_caps has ACPI_VIDEO_BACKLIGHT\n  - If yes, and not Win8 or no BACKLIGHT_RAW, return acpi_backlight_video\n  - Or if Win8 and BACKLIGHT_RAW, return acpi_backlight_native\n- So if video caps support backlight and not Win8, it would return acpi_backlight_video\n- And since it's not acpi_backlight_vendor, the acer-wmi brightness is disabled!\n\n\n- The code first sets the backlight type to vendor if the system is in the DMI table, then checks if the resulting type is vendor. This shows the condition checking whether the backlight type equals vendor is what gates acer-wmi's registration.
